# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Envoy Hot Restart Mechanism

## Your Task

Find all C++ source files in envoyproxy/envoy that implement the hot restart mechanism: the HotRestart interface, the parent/child process handshake, the socket passing via Unix domain sockets, the drain sequence, and the child process readiness signaling.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` (envoyproxy/envoy)
- `sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367` (envoyproxy/data-plane-api)
- `sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6` (envoyproxy/go-control-plane)
- `sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` (grpc/grpc)

Perfect! I've created a comprehensive answer file at `/workspace/answer.json` that documents all C++ source files implementing the hot restart mechanism in envoyproxy/envoy.

## Summary

The hot restart mechanism is implemented across **13 C++ files** organized into several key components:

### Core Files:
1. **Interface & Main Implementation**: `hot_restart.h`, `hot_restart_impl.h/cc`, `hot_restart_nop_impl.h`
2. **Protocol**: `hot_restart.proto` (defines request/reply message types)
3. **RPC Protocol**: `hot_restarting_base.h/cc` (Unix domain sockets with fd passing)
4. **Child Process**: `hot_restarting_child.h/cc` (socket duplication, drain signaling, stats merging)
5. **Parent Process**: `hot_restarting_parent.h/cc` (listening for requests, socket passing, stats export)
6. **OS Abstraction**: `os_sys_calls_hot_restart.h` and POSIX implementation

### Key Implementation Details:

- **Parent/Child Handshake**: Via Unix domain socket addresses computed from restart epoch
- **Socket Passing**: Using `SCM_RIGHTS` control data in `sendmsg()`/`recvmsg()`
- **RPC Protocol**: Custom serialization with 64-bit length prefix + protobuf payload over datagram sockets
- **Drain Sequence**: Parent listeners drain when child sends `DrainListeners` request
- **Child Readiness**: Child signals readiness by clearing `SHMEM_FLAGS_INITIALIZING` flag
- **Stats Merging**: Parent exports gauges, counter deltas, and dynamic stat metadata
- **UDP Forwarding**: Separate RPC channel for QUIC packet forwarding during drain
- **Shared Memory**: Process-shared pthread mutexes for log and access log synchronization

The answer.json file includes 20 key functions/methods in the execution chain, showing the flow from HotRestartImpl initialization through the entire handshake and communication protoc

\"HotRestartImpl::mergeParentStatsIfAny\"}\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"The hot restart mechanism in Envoy allows for graceful live restarting of the Envoy proxy without dropping connections. The implementation spans multiple C++ source files in github.com/envoyproxy/envoy:\\n\\n## Core Interface and Implementation\\n\\n**envoy/server/hot_restart.h** defines the abstract `HotRestart` interface with methods for draining parent listeners, duplicating parent listen sockets, registering UDP forwarding listeners, and merging parent stats.\\n\\n**source/server/hot_restart_impl.h** and **source/server/hot_restart_impl.cc** provide the main Linux implementation of hot restart. The `HotRestartImpl` class contains two internal instances (`as_child_` and `as_parent_`) to handle both parent and child roles. It also manages a `SharedMemory` structure used for inter-process coordination that includes version information, flags (like `SHMEM_FLAGS_INITIALIZING`), and process-shared pthread mutexes for logging synchronization.\\n\\n**source/server/hot_restart_nop_impl.h** provides a no-operation implementation used when hot restart is disabled.\\n\\n## Protocol Definition\\n\\n**source/server/hot_restart.proto** defines the `HotRestartMessage` protocol with request and reply message types. Requests include: `PassListenSocket` (to get a listening socket from parent), `ShutdownAdmin`, `Stats` (to request parent stats), `DrainListeners`, `Terminate`, `ForwardedUdpPacket` (for QUIC packet forwarding), and `TestConnection` (for connection testing). Replies include socket file descriptors, admin shutdown response with original start time, and aggregated statistics with counters, gauges, and dynamic stat metadata.\\n\\n## RPC Protocol and Socket Communication\\n\\n**source/server/hot_restarting_base.h** and **source/server/hot_restarting_base.cc** implement the core `RpcStream` class that handles the domain socket communication protocol. The protocol uses Unix domain sockets in datagram mode (`SOCK_DGRAM`) with a custom serialization format: a 64-bit network-byte-order length field followed by a protobuf message payload. Messages can span multiple datagrams up to 4096 bytes each. The `RpcStream` class implements `sendHotRestartMessage()` which serializes protobuf messages and sends them via `sendmsg()` with support for file descriptor passing via `SCM_RIGHTS` control data. The `receiveHotRestartMessage()` method uses `recvmsg()` to receive messages with optional blocking, buffering partial messages across multiple `recvmsg()` calls, and extracting passed file descriptors via `getPassedFdIfPresent()`. The base class `HotRestartingBase` maintains two `RpcStream` instances: `main_rpc_stream_` for main communication and `udp_forwarding_rpc_stream_` for UDP packet forwarding to avoid interference.\\n\\n## Child Process Implementation\\n\\n**source/server/hot_restarting_child.h** and **source/server/hot_restarting_child.cc** implement `HotRestartingChild` which handles the child process side of hot restart. The child is responsible for:\\n\\n- **Parent Connection**: Stores parent addresses computed from the restart epoch number\\n- **Socket Duplication**: Implements `duplicateParentListenSocket()` by sending a `PassListenSocket` request to the parent and extracting the returned file descriptor\\n- **Drain Signaling**: Implements `drainParentListeners()` by sending a `DrainListeners` request to notify the parent that the child is ready\\n- **Stats Merging**: Implements `getParentStats()` to request stats from the parent and `mergeParentStats()` to incorporate parent stats into the child's stats store\\n- **UDP Forwarding Context**: The `UdpForwardingContext` class maintains a map of registered UDP listeners to support QUIC packet forwarding from parent to child\\n- **Parent Drained Callbacks**: Implements `Network::ParentDrainedCallbackRegistrar` to allow listeners to register callbacks that fire when the parent finishes draining\\n- **Initialization**: The `initialize()` method sets up the `socket_event_udp_forwarding_` file event to handle incoming UDP packets from the parent\\n\\n## Parent Process Implementation\\n\\n**source/server/hot_restarting_parent.h** and **source/server/hot_restarting_parent.cc** implement `HotRestartingParent` and its nested `Internal` class. The parent process:\\n\\n- **Listens for Requests**: The `onSocketEvent()` method receives requests from the child and dispatches them\\n- **Socket Passing**: `getListenSocketsForChild()` locates the listening socket matching the child's request and passes the file descriptor back via `sendHotRestartMessage()` with fd control data\\n- **Admin Shutdown**: `shutdownAdmin()` shuts down admin processing and returns the original start time and reuse_port default setting\\n- **Stats Export**: `exportStatsToChild()` iterates over all sinks gauges and counters, latches counter values, and exports them along with dynamic stat metadata\\n- **Listener Draining**: `drainListeners()` initiates the drain sequence for all listeners\\n- **UDP Packet Forwarding**: The `handle()` method receives UDP packets and forwards them to the child via the UDP forwarding channel\\n\\n## Shared Memory and Synchronization\\n\\n**source/server/hot_restart_impl.h** defines the `SharedMemory` structure with `size_`, `version_`, and process-shared pthread mutexes for `log_lock_` and `access_log_lock_`. The `attachSharedMemory()` function in **source/server/hot_restart_impl.cc** manages the lifecycle of this shared memory segment using POSIX `shm_open()`, `mmap()`, and synchronization flags.\\n\\n## OS Abstraction\\n\\n**envoy/api/os_sys_calls_hot_restart.h** defines the abstract `HotRestartOsSysCalls` interface for shared memory operations (`shmOpen()`, `shmUnlink()`). **source/common/api/posix/os_sys_calls_impl_hot_restart.h** provides the POSIX implementation via `HotRestartOsSysCallsImpl`.\\n\\n## Key Mechanisms\\n\\n1. **Parent/Child Process Handshake**: Established via Unix domain socket addresses computed from the restart epoch number, allowing processes to discover each other\\n2. **File Descriptor Passing**: Used in `PassListenSocket` replies to transfer listening sockets from parent to child via `SCM_RIGHTS` control data in `recvmsg()`/`sendmsg()`\\n3. **Drain Sequence**: Initiated when child sends `DrainListeners`, triggering parent listeners to drain existing connections while child takes over new ones\\n4. **Child Readiness Signaling**: Child calls `drainParentListeners()` to signal that it has initialized, clearing the `SHMEM_FLAGS_INITIALIZING` flag so another new child can start\\n5. **Stats Merging**: Parent exports gauge values and counter deltas with dynamic stat name metadata so child can maintain continuity of metrics\\n6. **UDP Forwarding for QUIC**: Separate UDP forwarding RPC channel allows the parent to forward packets for connections the child should handle during draining\\n7. **Shared Memory Coordination**: The `SharedMemory` structure with atomic flags and process-shared mutexes synchronizes between parent and child processes\"\n}\n",

The parent process:\\n\\n- **Listens for Requests**: The `onSocketEvent()` method receives requests from the child and dispatches them\\n- **Socket Passing**: `getListenSocketsForChild()` locates the listening socket matching the child's request and passes the file descriptor back via `sendHotRestartMessage()` with fd control data\\n- **Admin Shutdown**: `shutdownAdmin()` shuts down admin processing and returns the original start time and reuse_port default setting\\n- **Stats Export**: `exportStatsToChild()` iterates over all sinks gauges and counters, latches counter values, and exports them along with dynamic stat metadata\\n- **Listener Draining**: `drainListeners()` initiates the drain sequence for all listeners\\n- **UDP Packet Forwarding**: The `handle()` method receives UDP packets and forwards them to the child via the UDP forwarding channel\\n\\n## Shared Memory and Synchronization\\n\\n**source/server/hot_restart_impl.h** defines the `SharedMemory` structure with `size_`, `version_`, and process-shared pthread mutexes for `log_lock_` and `access_log_lock_`. The `attachSharedMemory()` function in **source/server/hot_restart_impl.cc** manages the lifecycle of this shared memory segment using POSIX `shm_open()`, `mmap()`, and synchronization flags.\\n\\n## OS Abstraction\\n\\n**envoy/api/os_sys_calls_hot_restart.h** defines the abstract `HotRestartOsSysCalls` interface for shared memory operations (`shmOpen()`, `shmUnlink()`). **source/common/api/posix/os_sys_calls_impl_hot_restart.h** provides the POSIX implementation via `HotRestartOsSysCallsImpl`.\\n\\n## Key Mechanisms\\n\\n1. **Parent/Child Process Handshake**: Established via Unix domain socket addresses computed from the restart epoch number, allowing processes to discover each other\\n2. **File Descriptor Passing**: Used in `PassListenSocket` replies to transfer listening sockets from parent to child via `SCM_RIGHTS` control data in `recvmsg()`/`sendmsg()`\\n3. **Drain Sequence**: Initiated when child sends `DrainListeners`, triggering parent listeners to drain existing connections while child takes over new ones\\n4. **Child Readiness Signaling**: Child calls `drainParentListeners()` to signal that it has initialized, clearing the `SHMEM_FLAGS_INITIALIZING` flag so another new child can start\\n5. **Stats Merging**: Parent exports gauge values and counter deltas with dynamic stat name metadata so child can maintain continuity of metrics\\n6. **UDP Forwarding for QUIC**: Separate UDP forwarding RPC channel allows the parent to forward packets for connections the child should handle during draining\\n7. **Shared Memory Coordination**: The `SharedMemory` structure with atomic flags and process-shared mutexes synchronizes between parent and child processes\"\n}\n",
